A
TABLE
OF
THE TITLES OF THE PUBLIC GENERAL ACTS

and the FIRST SESSION of the SECOND PARLIAMENT OF

15 GEO . 5.— A.D. 1925 .
15 & 16 GEO . 5.-A.D. 1925
15 GEO , 5
1. An Act to amend the Education Act (Northern Ireland), 1923,
forthe purpose of removing doubts as to the provisionsof the
said Act with respect to voluntary religiousinstructionin
provided and transferredschools. (Education).
2. An Act to amend the Loans Guarantee Acts (Northern Ireland),
1922 to 1924,by increasingthe amount of loanswhich may be
guaranteedunder thoseActs, and extendingthe periodfor
giving guarantees thereunder. (Loans Guarantee).
3. An Act to enable the Ministry of Finance to make further
advances for dischargingthe liabilitiesof the Northern Irish
Unemployment Fund . (Unemployment Fund ).
4. An Act to apply certainSums out of the ConsolidatedFund of
Northern Ireland to the serviceof the year ended on the
thirty-firstday of March, nineteenhundred and twenty-four,
and of the years ending on the thirty-firstday of March ,
nineteen hundred and twenty-five, and the thirty-firstday of
March, nineteenhundred and twenty-six, and to appropriate
the suppliesgranted in thisSessionof Parliament. (Appropria-
tion).

## Page 4

iv. [15 & 16 GEO . 5.]Table of theStatutes.
15 & 16 GEO . 5 ,
1. An Act to enable regulationsto be made for the preventionof
danger arisingto publichealth in Northern Irelandfrom the
preparation, storageand distributionof milk. (PublicHealth,
Milk Regulations).
2. An Act to enable pensions and gratuitiesto be granted for
meritoriouspublic services. (Civil Pensions).
3. An Act to make furtherprovisionwith respectto the administra-
tionof certainpublicservicesin Northern Ireland, and for
purposes connected therewith. (AdministrativeProvisions).
4. An Act to provideforthe betteradministrationof the Charitable
Loan Societies(Ireland)Acts,1843 to 1906,in Northern Ireland,
and to amend the provisionsof the said Acts relatingto the
dispositionof surplus funds and property. (CharitableLoan
Societies).
5. An Act to establisha County Court Servicein Northern Ireland,
and to amend the Law relatingto certainCounty Officersand to
Courtsof QuarterSessionsand CivilBillCourts,and forpurposes
connected therewith. (County Officersand Courts).
6. An Act toamend ,initsapplicationtoNorthernIreland,theLaw
relatingto the Publicationof StatutoryRules and to the Laying
of StatutoryRules beforeParliament. (Rules Publication).
7. An Act to provide for the continuance of charging powers in
respectof canalor inlandnavigationundertakingsin Northern
Irelandofwhich possessionwas retainedortaken by the Minister
ofTransportunder the MinistryofTransportAct,1919. (Canals,
Continuanceof ChargingPowers).
8. An Act to establisha PharmaceuticalSocietyofNorthern Ireland;
to regulatethe qualificationsand provideforthe annuallicensing
of PharmaceuticalChemists, Chemists and Druggistsand
Druggists in Northern Ireland; to amend and extend the law
with respectto the sale of poisons; and for other purposes
incidentalthereto. (Pharmacy and Poisons).
9. An Act to alterthe rates of Estate Duty payable in Northern
Ireland. (Finance, EstatesDuty).
10. An Act to apply a Sum out ofthe ConsolidatedFund of Northern
Irelandto the serviceof the year ending on the thirty-firstday
of March ,nineteenhundred and twenty-six,and to appropriate
the SuppliesgrantedinthisSessionof Parliament. (Appropria-
tion).
11. An Act to empower the Governor of Northern Irelandto make
temporary provisionby Order in Councilforthe amendment of
the Unemployment Insurance Acts (Northern Ireland), 1920
to 1924. (Unemployment Insurance Temporary Provisions).

[15 & 16 GEO .5.] Table oftheStatutes. V.
12. An Act to amend and prolong the duration of the Increaseof
Rent and Mortgage Interest(Restrictions) Act, 1920, in its
applicationto Northern Ireland,and forpurposesin connection
therewith. (Rent and Mortgage InterestRestrictions).
13. An Act to amend the Housing Act (Northern Ireland), 1923,
and the Housing Acts Amendment Act (Northern Ireland),
1924. (Housing ).
14. An Act to enable the councilsof countiesand county boroughs
to make grants to the Queen's Universityof Belfast. (Local
Authorities, UniversityGrants).
15. An Act toenablethe MinistryofFinanceto make furtheradvances
fordischargingthe liabilitiesof the Northern IrishUnemploy-
ment Fund . (Unemployment Fund ).
16. An Act to amend the Dangerous Drugs Act , 1920, and the
Dangerous Drugs and Poisons (Amendment ) Act (Northern
Ireland), 1924, so far as is necessaryto assimilatethe law in
Northern Ireland to the law in force in Great Britain,in relation
to certaindangerous drugs ; and for purposes connected there-
with . (Dangerous Drugs ).
17. An Act to provideforthe establishmentof a Government Loans
Fund and the creationof UlsterLoans stock,and for purposes
connected therewith ; and to amend certain enactments relating
to the Exchequer and Finance. (Government Loans and
Exchequer Provisions).
18. An Act to make provisionwith respectto Salesand Loans made
for the purpose of the supply of Seed Potatoes to certain
occupiersand cultivatorsof land ir Northern Ireland. (Seed
PotatoesSupply).
19. An Act to continue certainExpiring Laws as respectsNorthern
Ireland. (Expiring Laws Continuance).
20.An Act toamend paragraph(3)ofsectiontwo and sub-section(I)
of sectionnine of the Old Age PensionsAct, 1908,in itsappli-
cation to Northern Ireland. (Old Age Pensions).
21. An Act for taking the Census for Northern Irelandin the year
nineteenhundred and twenty-six, and forotherwisecollecting
statisticalinformation . (Census ).
22. An Act to amend sub-section(2)ofsectionthreeofthe Unemploy-
ment Insurance(No. 2)Act (Northern Ireland),1924,to amend
the law with respectto the periodon the expirationof which
benefitunder the Acts relatingto unemployment insurance
becomes payable and with respectto the ratesof contribution
under the saidActs, and to continuethe saving contained in
sub-section(1)ofsectiontwelveofthe Unemployment Insurance
Act (Northern Ireland), 1923. (UnemploymentInsurance).

vi . [15 & 16 GEO . 5.]Table of theStatutes.
23.An Act tomake provisionforpensionsforwidows,orphans,and
personsbetween the ages of sixty-fiveand seventy,and forthe
payment of contributionsin respectthereof;and to amend the
enactments relatingto health and unemployment insurance
and old age pensions. (Widows ', Orphans' and Old Age Con-
tributoryPensions ).
24. An Act toempower countycouncilsto carryoutschemesforthe
drainage,and improvement by drainage,of lands; to provide
for the transferto county councilsof the functionsof certain
existingdrainage authorities; to enable furtherpowers to be
grantedto otherexistingdrainageauthorities;and to establish
a Drainage Advisory Committee ; and for other purposes con-
nectedtherewith. (Drainage).

Irelandto the serviceof the year ending on the thirty-firstday
ofMarch,nineteenhundredand twenty-six,and to appropriate
the further Supplies granted in this Session of Parliament.
(Appropriation(No. 2)).
26. An Act to enable the Ministry of Finance to make further
advances for dischargingthe liabilitiesof the Northern Irish
Unemployment Fund . (Unemployment Fund (No. 2)).
27. An Act to extend the powers of councilsof countiesand county
boroughs and urban districtcouncilsto borrow money for the
purposes of the Education Act (Northern Ireland), 1923.
(Education (Administrative Provisions) ).
28. An Act to amend the Superannuation Acts (Northern Ireland),
1921 to 1923. (Superannuation ).
29. An Act to increase the maximum rates at which charges are
leviableunder sectionthree of the IntoxicatingLiquor Act
(Northern Ireland), 1923, and to make furtherprovisionwith
respectto the repayment of advances made to the Claims Fund
establishedunder the said section, and with respect to the
payment of the saidcharges. (IntoxicatingLiquor (Finance)).
30. An Act to alter certain Duties of Excise and to amend the law
relatingto certainDuties of Inland Revenue ,and for purposes
connected therewith. (Finance).

and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-

CHAPTER 2 .
An Act to amend the Loans Guarantee Acts
(Northern Ireland),1922 to 1924,by increasing
the amount ofloanswhich may be guaranteed
under those Acts ,and extending the period for
giving guarantees thereunder .
B
[13th March , 1925.]
E it enacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1.- (1) The maximum limiton the aggregatecapital
amount of the loans, the principalor interestof which
may be guaranteed under the Loans Guarantee Acts
(Northern Ireland),1922 to 1924,shallbe increasedfrom
fivemillionpounds to six millionpounds .
(2) The power to give guarantees under the said
Acts may be exercisedat any time up to and including
the thirty-firstday of March, nineteenhundred and
twenty -six.
2. This Act may be cited as the Loans Guarantee
Act (Northern Ireland), 1925, and the Loans Guarantee
Acts (Northern Ireland), 1922 to 1924,and thisAct may
be citedtogetheras the Loans Guarantee Acts (Northern
Ireland), 1922 to 1925.

and the Senate and the House of Commons of

and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1. The Unemployment Fund Act (Northern Ireland),
1922, as amended by sectionfiveof the Unemployment

shallhave effectas if in the provisoto sub-section(1)
of sectionone of the first-mentioned Act three million
pounds were substitutedfor two milliontwo hundred
and fiftythousand pounds as the limit on the total
amount of advances which may be made under the first-
mentioned Act by the Ministry of Finance for dis-
charging the liabilitiesof the Northern Irishunemploy-

[15 & 16 GEO . 5.]
CHAPTER 1 .
An Act to enable regulations to be made for
the prevention of danger arising to public
health in Northern Ireland from the prepara-
tion,storage and distribution of milk .
BE
[21st May , 1925].
E it enacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
A.D. 1925 ,
of Ministry
ofHome
Affairsasto
7Edw.7,
c.32.
milk .
1. The Ministry of Home Affairsfor Northern Regulations
Irelandshallmake regulationsunder the Public Health
(Regulations as to Food ) Act , 1907, for the prevention
ofdangerarisingto publichealthfrom the preparation,
storage and distribution of milk intended for sale for
human consumption or for use in the manufacture of
products for human consumption ; and sub-section(1)
of sectionone of the said Act shall, for the purpose
aforesaid,have effectas though at the end thereofthe
followingparagraph were added :-
(d) provide for the manner in which any tin or
otherreceptaclecontainingdriedor condensed
milk isto be labelledor marked ,and prescribe
the minimum percentagesofmilk fatand milk
solids in dried or condensed milks .
2. This Act may be cited as the Public Health
(Milk Regulations) (Northern Ireland)Act ,1925.

CHAPTER 5 .
An Act to establisha County Court Service in
Northern Ireland , and to amend the Law re-
lating to certain County Officersand to Courts
of Quarter Sessions and Civil BillCourts , and
forpurposes connected therewith.
BE
[9th June , 1925.]
E itenactedby theKing'smost ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
PART I. COUNTY COURT SERVICE .
1.-(1) There shallbe establisheda county court
service for the several counties and counties of cities in
Northern Ireland, which serviceshall, subject to the
provisionsof thisAct, includeallpersonsappointedor
admitted theretoin the capacityof Clerk of the Crown
and Peace forany county or county of a city, or in the
capacityof an officer,clerk,or servant,under the direc-
tion or control of a Clerk of the Crown and Peace .
(2) The county courtserviceshallbe concernedwith
the dischargeof such functionsconnected with the busi-
nessofthe county court,or attachedto the officeofClerk
of the Crown and Peace ,as relateto Irishserviceswithin
10& 11Geo. the meaning ofthe Government ofIrelandAct ,1920.5 ,с.67 ,
(3) The Governor of Northern Irelandshall,subject
tothe provisionsofthisAct,have power toappoint tothe
county courtserviceforeach county orcounty of a citya
Clerk of the Crown and Peace and such other officers,
clerksand servantsas the said Governor may consider
necessaryfortheproperdischargeofthefunctionsofthat
service, having regard to the recommendations of the
Minister of Home AffairsforNorthern Ireland,and (so far
as relatesto numbers , salariesand remuneration) of the
Minister of Finance for Northern Ireland .
Any person may , notwithstanding anything con-
& 41Vict. tainedin the County Officersand Courts(Ireland) Act,
1877, be removed from the county court serviceby the

(4) Every person employed in the county court

with his consent; and every such person may be pro-

PART II .
PROVISIONS AS TO EXISTING OFFICERS .
7.-(1) The personwho isat the date ofthepassing
of thisAct the RegistrarforBelfastmay , ifhe so elects
within twelve months after that date , be admitted to
the county court service.
(2) Every person employed at the date of the
passingof thisAct by or under any Clerk of the Crown
and Peace and having been on the twenty -firstday of
October, nineteen hundred and twenty -four, and after
attaining the age of seventeen years, so employedfor a period of, or for periods amounting in
the aggregate to, seven years, and bound while so
employed to devote his whole time to the dutiesof his
office, may within twelve months afterthe passing of
thisAct electto be employed inthe county courtservice:
Provided that no such person shallbe admitted to
the county court serviceunlessthe Lord Chief Justice
of Northern Ireland has , with the concurrence of the
Ministry of Finance of Northern Ireland, certifiedthat
he is a fitand proper person to be employed in that
service;
Provided alsothat, in calculatingfor the purposes
of thissub-sectionthe durationof any periodof employ-
ment , any periods, not exceeding in the aggregate four
years,ofserviceby a personin any ofHis Majesty'snaval,
militaryor airforcesin the latewar shallbe treatedas
employment of that person by or under a Clerk of the
Crown and Peace .
(3) Every person who is admitted to the county
court serviceshallbecome subjectto the provisionsof

SCHEDULE .
Modificationsof Superannuation Acts in the case of a Clerk of the
Crown and Peace and the RegistrarforBelfast.
1. In the case of a Clerk of the Crown and Peace-
(a) the followingscaleshallbe substitutedforthe scaleof
superannuation allowances contained in section two of the
Superannuation Act, 1859 :—
To any such Clerk who shallhave servedseven years and
upwards and under eightyears,an annual allowanceof
seven forty-fifthsof the annual salaryand emoluments
of his office :
For eightyears,and under nine years,an annual allowance
ofeightforty-fifthsofsuch salaryand emoluments :
And in like manner a further addition to the annual allow-
ance of one forty-fifthin respectofeach additionalyear
of such service, untilthe completion of a period of
serviceof thirtyyears, when the annual allowanceof
thirtyforty-fifthsmay be granted ; and no addition
shallbe made in respectof any servicebeyond thirty
years .
“
(b) sectionten of the SuperannuationAct ,1859,shallhave
effectas if the words sixty-five years" were substituted
thereinfor" sixtyyears," and such Clerkshallvacatehis office
at the age ofseventy-two years ;
(c) the provisionsof sectionsone to four (inclusive) of the
SuperannuationAct, 1909,shallnot apply.
2. In the case of the Registrarfor Belfast-
(a) sectionten of the SuperannuationAct,1859,shallhave
effectasifthe words " sixty-fiveyears" were substitutedtherein
for" sixtyyears," and such Registrarshallvacatehis officeat
the age of seventy-two years;
(b) no deduction from the amount of the additionalallow.
ance or gratuitypayable under sectionone or sectiontwo of the
Superannuation Act, 1909,shallbe made for any years served
by such Registrarafterattainingthe age of sixty-fiveyears.
CHAPTER 6 .
An Act to amend ,in its applicationto Northern
Ireland, the Law relating to the Publication
ofStatutory Rules and to the Laying of Statu-
toryRules beforeParliament. [9th June ,1925.]
B
E it enacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-

## Page 39

[15 & 16 GEO .5.] Rules PublicationAct 33[Ch . 6.]
(Northern Ireland),1925.
1.-(1)Allstatutoryrulesmade afterthepassingof
thisAct shallforthwithafterthey aremade be sentto the
officerforthetime beingappointedto printthe Acts of
the Parliament of Northern Ireland(in thisAct referred
toas "the Government Printer")and shall,in accordance
with the provisionscontainedinthe Scheduleto thisAct,
and subjectto any regulationswhich may be made under
the powersconferredby thisAct,be numbered,printed
and sold by the Government Printer.
(2) Any statutoryrulesmay , without prejudiceto
any othermode of citation,be citedby the number given
to them in pursuance of sub-section(1) of thissection
and the calendar year.
(3) Where any statutoryrulesare requiredin pur-
suance of any Act (whether passedbeforeor afterthe
passingof thisAct) to be publishedor notifiedin the
Belfast Gazette , a notice in that Gazette of the rules
having been made ,and ofthe placewhere copiesof them
can be purchased,shallbe sufficientcompliance with the
said requirement .
(4) Regulations may be made by the Ministry of
Finance for Northern Ireland,with the concurrence of the
Lord ChiefJusticeof Northern Irelandand the Speakers
of the Senate and the House of Commons of Northern
Ireland,forprescribingany matterrequiredby thisAct
to be prescribedby regulationsand generallyforgiving
full effect to this Act .
(5) Any matter or questionwhich isrequiredto be
determinedin pursuanceof thisAct, and any question
which ariseson the applicationof any provisionof this
Act toany exerciseofa statutorypower ortoany statutory
rules,shallbe referredto the saidMinistryofFinance and
determined by that Ministry,with the concurrenceofthe
said Lord ChiefJusticeand Speakers.
2.- (1) The statutory rules to which this Act
appliesare those made under any Act (whether passed
by the Parliament of Northern Irelandor by the Parlia-
ment oftheUnitedKingdom )by a rule-making authority
as in thissectiondefined, and relatingto any matter in
respect of which the Parliament of Northern Ireland has
power to make laws.

Section 1 (1.)
SCHEDULE ,
PROVISIONS AS TO PUBLICATION OF STATUTORY RULES
1. Allstatutoryruleswhen sentto the Government Printershall
be numbered consecutively,as nearlyas may be,in the orderin which
they are receivedby the Government Printer.
2. There shallbe a separateseriesof numbers foreach calendar
year,and allstatutoryrulesmade in any year shallwherever possible
be numbered withthestatutoryrulesofthatyear and included(subject
totheprovisionshereinaftercontainedinthisSchedule)intheannual
volume of that year.

## Page 43

[15 & 16 GEO .5.] Rules PublicationAct 37[Ch . 6, 7.]
(NorthernIreland),1925.
3. Allstatutoryrulesshallbe printedand soldunless,inthe case
of rulesnot requiredto be publishedin the BelfastGazette,the rule-
making authoritydeclaresthatitisunnecessaryto printand sellthem ,
and such declarationisnot over-ruledby the determinationof a ques.
tion under this Act .
4. An annual volume of statutoryrules shallbe prepared and
published.
5. In the annual volume a distinction shall be made between
statutoryruleswhich are generaland thosewhich arelocal,following
(unless in exceptional circumstances) the distinctionadopted
between public generalActs and localActs of Parliament; and in
that volume the generalrulesshallbe printed at length and lists
shall be included of :-
(a) the localrules;
(b) any generalrulesnot printed by reason of a declaration
under Article 3 of this Schedule ; and
(c) any temporary statutoryrulesexcluded from publication
at lengthunder Article8 of thisSchedule.
6. The rule-making authority, in sending any statutoryruleto
the Government Printer,shallstate whether itconsidersthe rule to be
generalor local,and that statementshallbe followedunlessover-ruled
by the determinationof a questionunder thisAct .
7. In the annual volume of statutoryrulesthegenerairulesshall
be publishedin a classifiedform, that is to say, grouped under an
alphabeticallyarranged seriesof headings of law,the headings being
so far as possibleidenticalwith such headingsas may be adopted for
an Index to the Statutes in force in Northern Ireland .
8. Articles1 and 3 of thisSchedule shallapply to temporary
statutoryrules,but ifthoseruleshave ceasedto be inforceat the time
of the publicationof the annual volume,or willso ceasea shorttime
afterwards,they may be excluded from publicationat length in that
volume,subjectto thedeterminationof a questionunderthisAct
in case of any differencebetween the rule-making authorityand the
Government Printer .
A.D. 1925 .

PART I. A.D. 1925,
CONSTITUTION AND GENERAL POWERS OF THE PHARMA-

1.-( 1) There shallbe establisheda Societyto be Constitution
calledthe Pharmaceutical Society of Northern Ireland
and to be constituted as hereinafter in this section
mentioned ; and that Society(in thisAct referredto as
" the Society") shallbe a body corporateby the name
aforesaidwith perpetualsuccessionand a common seal,
and with power to acquire and hold land for the purposes
of this Act without licence in mortmain .
(2) The sealof the Societyshallbe authenticated
in such manner as may be prescribed,and any document
purportingto be sealedwith the said sealso authenti-
cated shallbe receivablein evidence of the particulars
stated in that document .
(3) The persons to be nominated in that behalf
under the provisions of Part I. of the First Schedule to
this Act , and allother persons who shallbe qualified
and electedin accordancewith the provisionsofthisAct,
shallbe members of the Society.
(4) There shallbe a Councilof the Society(in thisAct referredto as " the Council") and a Presidentand
Vice-President of the Council; and the persons to be
nominated in that behalf under the provisions of Part II.
of the First Schedule to thisAct shallbe respectively
the President,Vice-President and members of the Council
on its first constitution .

FirstSchedule to thisAct shallapply,except as herein-

Council .

30. In this Act , unless the context otherwise re-
quires-
The expression" prescribed means prescribed
by regulationsmade by the Counciland approved
by the Ministerof Home Affairs:
The expression" existing" where used inrelation
to a pharmaceuticalchemist, registeredchemist
and druggist, registereddruggist, or registeredassistantto a pharmaceutical chemist, means
registeredin the appropriate register existing
immediately before the passing of thisAct under
and forthepurposesofthePharmacy Act (Ireland)
1875, and the Pharmacy Act (Ireland), 1875,
Amendment Act,1890,and theexpression" existing
register," where used inrelationto any such person
means the appropriateregisteraforesaid.

means the Minister of Home Affairs for Northern
Ireland, and the expression " Ministry of HomeAffairs" means the Ministry of Home Affairsfor
Northern Ireland ;
The expression" MinistryofFinance " means the
Ministry of Finance for Northern Ireland:The expression " poison" means all articles
deemed to be poisons and specifiedin the Fourth
Schedule to this Act , or added to that Schedule
under the provisions of Part IV . of thisAct .

PROVISIONS AS TO THE ELECTION OF PRESIDENT , VICE- Section1(5).

member ofthe Council,or by hisresignationof suchofficeor incapacity
tohold it,such vacancy shallbe filledby theelectionof some member
of the Council to hold such office.
2. (1) The members of the Councilwho are representativesof
the Queen's Universityof Belfastand of the Medical Committee of
Northern Ireland (or other body recognisedin lieuthereofunder
Part IIof thisSchedule) and of the wholesaledrug tradein Northern
Irelandshallhold officeforthreeyearsfrom the date of theirnomina-
tionand shallbe eligibleforre-nomination.
On the expirationof the saidperiodof threeyears,and of each
subsequentperiodof threeyears,the saidUniversityand Committee
or otherbody shallrespectivelynominate, to representthem fora
furtherperiodofthreeyears,the same number ofpersonsasisprovided
in Part II of thisSchedule, and the Ministerof Home Affairsshall
nominate for such furtherperiod one person to representthe said
wholesaledrug trade.
(2) The members of the Council,otherthan those referredto in
sub-section(1)ofthisArticle,shallgo out ofofficeduringeach periodof
threeyearsfrom the passingof thisAct by rotationin the following
manner :-
(a) On the firstMonday ofOctoberinthefirstyear afterthe pass-
ingofthisAct ,one-third,as near as may be,ofthe members
of the Councilwho are members of the Societyby virtueof
Part I.of thisSchedule,and one-third,as near as may be,
of thedruggists'representativeson the Council,shallgo out
of office ;
(b) On the firstMonday of Octoberinthefollowingyearthe same
number of members of the Council who are members of the
Societyby virtueof Part I.of thisSchedule and druggists'
representativeson the Council, respectively, shallgo out
of office ;
(c) On the firstMonday of Octoberinthe year followingthe year
mentioned in the precedingparagraph,the remainingmem-
bersoftheCouncilto whom thissub-sectionapplies,and who
have been inofficefrom the beginningofthe triennialperiod,
shallgo out of office;
(d) The same procedureshallbe followedduring each triennial
period,and ineach instancetheplaceoftheretiringmembers
shallbe suppliedby electionon the firstMonday in October
oftheyearinwhich theretirementtakesplace.
The members of the Council who are to be elected under
thissub-sectionshallbe electedby the members and associ-
atesofthe Societyvotingas one body .

4. In orderto determinetherotationby which the firstmembers
of the Councilshallgo out ofoffice,the Councilshallat theirfirstmeet-
ing form a rotationlist,and at that meeting the chairman shallwrite
the names of allthe members on separateslipsofpaper of,as nearlyas
may be,equalsize,and havingfoldedthem up inthesame manner he
shallput them intoa ballotbox and shall,inthepresenceofthemeeting
draw out the slipsof paper in successionand the names upon the slips
sodrawn shallbe writtenby the chairman ina listinthe orderinwhich
they aredrawn . Every such listshallbe enteredinthe minutesofthe
Council,and the names thereinshallbe numbered consecutively,and
the members of the Council shall retire from officein the order in which
theirnames appear on such listin the proportionshereinbeforemen-
tioned in this Part .
5. Every member of the Councilgoing out of officeby rotation
may be re-elected, and afterre-electionhe shallfor the purposes of
rotation be considered as a new member .
6. If any extraordinaryvacancy occursintheCouncil(exceptin
the caseof a member to whom sub-section(1) of Article2 ofthisPart
applies),the Councilshall,on a day to be appointedby the President
(not beinglaterthan thesecondordinarymeeting afterthe vacancy has
been signifiedto the President)electto fillthe vacancy a member of
the Society, if the vacancy occurs amongst those members , or an
associateof the Society,ifthe vacancy occursamongst the druggists'
representativeson the Council. Every personso electedshallcontinue
a member of the Counciluntilthe time when the person in the room
ofwhom he was chosenwould regularlyhave gone out ofoffice,and he
shallthen go out ofofficebut shallbe capableofimmediate re-election.
If any extraordinaryvacancy occurs amongst the members of
the Councilto whom sub-section(1) of Article2 of thisPart applies,
the saidUniversity,Committee or otherbody ,or Minister(as the case
may require)shallnominate anotherrepresentativeto fillthe vacancy
for the unexpiredportionofthe term of officeof the member in whose
room such representativeisnominated .
7. Elections of members of the Council and of the President and
Vice-Presidentshallbe held,and thevotingand otherproceedingsinthe
caseofa contestshallbe conducted,insuchmanner asmay be prescribed.
8. At a meeting ofthe Councilthe President,or in his absence
theVice-President,shallactas chairman,and ifboth the Presidentand
Vice-President are absent one of the members present shallbe elected
chairman by the majoritypresent.
9. At allmeetingsofthe Councilthe questionsthereconsidered
shallbe decidedby a majority; in the case of an equal division, the
Chairman shall,in additionto hisown vote,have a castingvote.
10. No businessshallbe conducted at any meetings of the
Councilunlessseven members of the Councilbe present, and all
powersvestedintheCouncilby orunderthisAct may beexercisedby
any seven or more of the Councilpresentat any meeting thereof.

CHAPTER 9 .
An Act to alterthe rates of Estate Duty payable
in Northern Ireland . [9th June , 1925.]
BEE it enacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1.-(1) The scaleset out in the Schedule to this
Act shall, in the case of persons dying afterthe com-
mencement of thisAct , be substitutedfor the scaleset
out in the Third Schedule to the Finance Act , 1919 , as
the scaleof ratesof estateduty :
Provided that, where an interestin expectancy
withinthe meaning of Part I of the Finance Act , 1894,
in any propertyhas,before the fourteenthday of May ,
nineteenhundred and twenty-five,been bonâ fidesoldor
mortgaged for fullconsiderationin money or money's
worth, then no other duty on that property shallbe
payableby thepurchaseror mortgageewhen theinterest
fallsintopossessionthan would havebeenpayableifthis
Act had not passed,and in the caseof a mortgage any
higher duty payable by the mortgagor shallrank as a
charge subsequent to that of the mortgagee.

land), 1923 , and the Housing Acts Amendment

CHAPTER 14 .
An Act to enable the councils of counties and
county boroughs to make grants to the Queen's
University of Belfast. [9th June ,1925.]
B
E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityofthesame,as follows:-
1.- (1) The councilof any county or county bor-
ough in Northern Irelandshallhave power to place any
sums at the disposal of the Queen's University of
Belfastto be appliedforany educationalpurposeswhich
the council may consider willbenefittheircounty or
borough .
(2) Any expenses incurredfor the purposes of this
Act shall, ifincurredby the councilof a county other
than a county borough, be defrayedout of the county
fund as a county at largecharge and ,ifincurredby the
councilof a county borough,be defrayed out of any rate
or fund applicableto the purposes of the Public Health
(Ireland) Acts, 1878 to 1918, or out of any other rate
or fund which the Ministryof Home Affairsmay ,on the
applicationofthecouncil,approve.
2. This Act may be citedas the Local Authorities
(UniversityGrants) Act (Northern Ireland), 1925.

CHAPTER 17 .
An Act to Provide for the establishment of a
Government Loans Fund and the creation of
Ulster Loans stock, and forpurposes connected.
therewith ; and to amend certain enactments
relating to the Exchequer and Finance .
BE
[20th October, 1925.]
E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:---

## Page 103

[15 & 16 GEO .5.] Government Loans and 97[Ch . 17.]
Exchequer ProvisionsAct
(Northern Ireland), 1925.
PART I.
GOVERNMENT LOANS FUND AND ULSTER
LOANS STOCK .
1.-(1) The advance by the Ministryof Finance of
money forthe purposeof any of the loansor advances
describedin the Scheduleto thisAct (inthisAct referred
to as " Government Loans "), shallbe subject to the
authorityof an annual Act of Parliament ; and when
Parliament has authorisedany advances forthe purpose
of Government Loans , the Ministry of Finance shall,
from time to time, issuefor that purpose such sums as
may be forthetime beingrequiredtherefor,not exceeding
in the aggregatethe amount authorisedby the annual
Act .
All Government Loans shall be issued out of the
Government Loans Fund establishedby thisAct,and not
out of the Exchequer , and any enactments applicable
immediately beforethe passingofthisAct to Government
Loans,and providingforthe issueofsuch Loans from the
Exchequer , shallhave effectaccordingly.
(2) Ifthe annual Act authorisingadvances ofmoney
for Government Loans fixesa period during which the
money is to be issued, the said money shallbe issued
by the Ministryof Finance during that period and not
subsequent to it.
(3) Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing
provisionsof thissection,the Ministryof Finance may ,
on or before the thirty-firstday of March , nineteen
hundred and twenty-seven, issue for the purpose of
Government Loans such sums as will not exceed , when
taken togetherwith any sums advanced forthatpurpose
before the passingof thisAct-
(a) the aggregatesum of eighthundred and fifty
thousand pounds, in respectof the Loans
describedin paragraphs1, 2 and 3 of the
Schedule to this Act ; and
(b) the aggregatesum of one million,one hundred
and fiftythousand pounds , in respectof all
other Loans describedin the said Schedule,
but so, in any case, that any limit placed by Act of
Parliamentupon the amount of any such Government
Loan be not exceeded .

Finance may , from time to time, createa capitalstock
yieldingdividends at the prescribedrate per cent. per
annum on the nominal amount of the capital (which
stock is in thisAct referredto as " Ulster Loans stock." )
(2) Equal half-yearly dividends shallbe payable

paid out of the Government Loans Fund ; and , ifthat
Fund is insufficient,the dividends shall,to the extent of

provided by this Act.
(3) The Ulster Loans stock shall be redeemable
afterthe expirationof such periodas may be prescribed
forthe purpose of redemption,but so that each issueof
the stock shallbe redeemed at the expirationof fifty
years from the date of its creation.

CHAPTER 18 .
An Act to make provision with respect to Sales
and Loans made forthe purpose of the supply
ofSeed Potatoes to certainoccupiersand culti-
vators of land in Northern Ireland ,
BE
[10th November ,1925.]
E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-

## Page 115

[15 & 16 GEO .5.] Seed PotatoesSupply Act [Ch .18.] 109
(Northern Ireland), 1925.
1.- (1) Where , at any time between the firstday
of January,nineteenhundred and twenty-five,and the
firstday ofJuly,nineteenhundred and twenty-five,the
guardians of any union have , with the sanctionof the
Ministryof Home Affairs, provideda supply of seed
potatoesfor the use of any districtelectoraldivisionof
theirunion, and have soldany such potatoesto any
occupieror cultivatorof land in that electoraldivision,
the saleshallbe deemed to have been legallymade ,and
any sum due to the guardianson account thereofshallbe
paid by two equal instalments, and the guardians shall
certifythe amount of each instalmentto the councilof
the county comprisingthe electoraldivisionaffected.
(2) For obtainingpayment of each instalmentdue
from any personthe county councilshalllevythe amount ,
where the person israted to the poor rate,by a special
rateto be added to the poor rate assessedon the tene-
ments occupied by him and to be collectedtherewith.
(3) Where any such personisnot ratedto the poor
rate,the county councilshallmake a specialrateforthe
purposes of thisAct to which he shallbe rated.
(4) Every suchlast-mentionedspecialrateshallbe
recoverable in the same manner and with the same
remedies by the collectorsof the poor rate as ifitwere
poor rate,and shallbe paid by the county councilto the
guardians .
(5) Where the poor rateiscollectedintwo moieties
the specialraterequiredforthe purposesofthisAct shall
be collectedwith the firstmoiety of the poor rate.
(6) The firstofthespecialratesrequiredforthepur-
poses of thisAct shallbe made at the same time as the
firstordinary poor rate made during the year nineteen
hundred and twenty-six, and the second of those rates
shallbe made at the same time as the firstordinarypoor
ratemade during the year nineteenhundred and twenty-
seven .
A.D 1925

money isinsufficient,then out ofallmoneys subsequently
receivedby him on account of the guardians, pay the
amount specifiedin the orderto the MinistryofFinance.

disqualifiedunder any articlein the schedule to the
Local Government (Application of Enactments ) Order,
1898,by reasonof hishaving enteredintoa contractfor
the purchase of seed potatoesunder thisAct .

and thingsdone by the Ministryof Home Affairsin rela-
tion to the provisionduring the periodin that behalfin
thisAct mentioned of seed potatoesby the guardiansof
any union shallbe, and be deemed to have been, valid
and effectualfor allpurposes.
5. This Act may be cited as the Seed Potatoes
Supply Act (Northern Ireland),1925.

CHAPTER 19 ,
An Act to continue certain Expiring Laws as
respects Northern Ireland .
[10th November , 1925.]
WHEREASJHEREAS the Acts (whether passed by the Parlia-
ment of the United Kingdom or by the
Parliament of Northern Ireland) mentioned in the
Schedule to thisAct are,in so far as they are in forcein
Northern Irelandand are temporary in theirduration,
limitedto expire on the severaldates specifiedin the
several Parts of the said Schedule in connection with such
Acts respectively:
And whereas itisexpedientto provideforthecontinuance
as in thisAct mentioned of those Acts ,and of the enact-
ments amending or affectingthe same :
Be it thereforeenacted by the King's most Excellent
Majesty, and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Ireland in this presentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityofthe same ,asfollows:-
A.D. 1925 .
of Acts in
Schedule .
1. (1) The Acts mentioned in the severalParts of Continuance
the Schedule to thisAct shall,to the extent specifiedin
column three of that Schedule, be continued as respects
Northern Irelanduntilthe thirty-firstday of December ,
nineteenhundred and twenty-six, and shallthen expire
unless further continued .
(2) Any unrepealedenactments amending or affect-
ing the enactments continuedby thisAct shall,in so far
as they are temporary in theirduration, be continued in
likemanner ,whether they are mentioned in the Schedule
to this Act or not .
2.-(1) ThisAct may be citedasthe ExpiringLaws Shorttitle
Continuance Act (Northern Ireland), 1925.
(2) References in thisAct to any enactments of the
Parliament of the United Kingdom shallbe construedas
referencesto thoseenactments as they apply in Northern
Ireland .
(3) Nothing inthisAct shallbe construedas affect-
ingany enactment in sofar asthe enactment relatesto a
matter with respectto which the Parliament of Northern
Irelandhas not power to make laws.

CHAPTER 20 .

and sub -section (1) of section nine of the Old

BEE itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin this presentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-

## Page 122

116 Old Age PensionsAct [15 & 16 GEC .5.][Ch .20.]
1
4
A.D. 1925 .
Amendment
of statutory
condition as
to means .
8 Edw . 7 ,
c .40 ;
9& 10 Geo .5 ,
c. 102 ,
Amendment
of law as to
penalty for
false state-
ments ,& c.
Short title .
(Northern Ireland), 1925.
1.-(1) Paragraph(3)ofsectiontwo oftheOld Age
Pensions Act, 1908, as amended by sub-section(1) of
sectiontwo of the Old Age Pensions Act , 1919 (which
contains the statutory conditionsas to means ), shall
for allpurposes have effectas though afterthe words
" calculated under this Act " there were inserted the
words " afterdeducting therefrom such part, if any ,
thereof,but not exceedingin any casethirty-ninepounds ,
as isderivedfrom any sourceotherthan earnings" ;
Provided that no personcoming withinthe descrip-
tion set out in column I. of the Schedule to this Act shall be
entitledto obtainunder the Old Age PensionsActs,1908
to 1919 , a pension at a rate higher than the rate of such
pension(ifany)as he would have been entitledto obtain
ifthisAct had not been passed,unlesshe isa person who
has the qualificationprescribedby column II. of the
said Schedule .
(2) Referencesin thisAct to the Old Age Pensions
Acts, 1908 to 1919, or any enactments thereofshallbe
construed as references to those Acts or enactments as
they apply in Northern Ireland.
(3) This sectionshallcome intooperationon the first
day of Aprilnineteenhundred and twenty-six.
2.Notwithstandingany provisionin any Act
prescribingthe periodwithinwhich summary proceedings
may be commenced , proceedingsfor an offenceunder
sub-section(1)ofsectionnineofthe Old Age PensionsAct ,
1908,may be commenced atany time withinthreemonths
from the date on which evidence,sufficientinthe opinion
ofthe MinisterofFinance to justifya prosecutionforthe
offence, comes to his knowledge , or within six months
afterthe commission of the offence, whichever period is
the longer.
For the purposesofthe foregoingprovisiona certi-
ficatepurportingto be signedby the saidMinister,or by
a secretaryor assistantsecretaryof the Ministryof Fin-
ance , as to the date on which such evidence as aforesaid
came to the knowledge of the saidMinistershallbe con-
clusive evidence of that date .
3. This Act may be citedas the Old Age Pensions
Act (Northern Ireland),1925,and the Old Age Pensions

CHAPTER 21 .

Ireland in the year nineteen hundred and

the year nineteenhundred and twenty -sixin the manner
hereinafterdirectedand the censusday shallbe Sunday

day , being Sunday , as may be fixedby the Governor of

(NorthernIreland),1925.
CHAPTER 23 .
An Act to make provisionforpensionsforwidows ,
orphans,and persons between the ages of sixty
fiveand seventy,and forthe payment ofcontri-
butions in respect thereof; and to amend the
enactments relatingto health and unemploy-
ment insurance and old age pensions.
B
[6th November ,1925.]
E itenacted by the King's most Excellent Majesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
ContributoryPensions.
1.-(1) Subjectto the provisionsof thisAct
relatingto the payment of contributions(includingpay-
ments out of moneys provided by Parliament) and
otherwise, pensionsshallbe payableas follows, thatis
to say-
(a) tothe widow ofan insuredman a pensionatthe
rateoftenshillingsper week ,with an additional
allowanceinrespectofchildrenwhileunder the
age hereinafterspecified, at the rate of five
shillingsper week for the eldestor only such
child, and three shillingsper week for eachothersuch child(inthisAct calleda " widow's
pension") ;
(b) in respectof the orphan childrenwhileunder
the age hereinafterspecifiedof an insured man
or of an insuredwidow , a pension at the rate
of seven shillingsand sixpence per week for
each such child(inthisAct calledan " orphan's
pension" );
(c) to an insuredman or an insured woman who
has attainedthe age of sixty-fivebut has not
attainedthe age of seventy,and to the wife of
an insured man who has attainedthe age of
sixty-five(such wife having attainedthe age
of sixty-fivebut not having attainedthe age

Widows ' and Orphans' Pensions.

or districtcharge, according as the Ministry
of Home Affairsmay direct;
(b) in the case of a county borough, borough or
districtcouncil,as part ofthe generalexpenses
of the council in the execution of the Public
Health (Ireland)Acts,1878 to 1918.
(5) For the purposes of thisAct the Ministry of
Home Affairsor Ministryof Education (as the case may
require) may , at the request of the Ministryof Labour ,
referto the localauthorityfor investigationand report
any matter relatingto a widow or childto or in respect
of whom a widow's or orphan's pension or additional
allowance is payable.

THIRD SCHEDULE .
DISQUALIFICATIONS FOR RECEIPT OF PENSION .
1. A person shallbe disqualifiedfor receivingor continuing
to receivea pension,notwithstandingthefulfilmentof thestatutory
conditions-
(a) whilehe isan inmate of any workhouse or other poor-law
institution :
Provided that a person who has become an inmate
of any workhouse or other poor-law institutionfor the
purposeof obtainingmedicalor surgicaltreatmentshall
not, during a period of three months from the date on
which he becomes such an inmate ifhe so long continues
to requiresuch treatment, be disqualifiedon the ground
only that he issuch an inmate forreceivingor continuing
to receivea pension;
(b) while he is detained in any lunatic asylum within the
meaning of the Local Government (Ireland) Act , 1898, or
while he is being maintained in any place as a pauper or
criminal lunatic .
2. Where a personhas been beforethe passingof thisAct ,or is
afterthe passingof thisAct ,convictedof any offence,and ordered
to be imprisonedwithout the optionof a fineor to sufferany greater
punishment,he shallbe disqualifiedforreceivingor continuingto
receivea pensionwhilehe isdetainedin prisonin consequenceof the
order .

(NorthernIreland),1925.
CHAPTER 24 .
An Act to empower county councils to carry out
schemes forthe drainage, and improvement by
drainage, of lands ; to provide for the transfer
to county councils of the functions of certain
existingdrainage authorities; to enable further
powers to be granted to other existingdrainage
authorities;and to establisha Drainage Advis-
ory Committee ;and forotherpurposes connected
therewith . [10th November ,1925.]
BEE itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
PART I.
POWERS OF COUNTY COUNCILS TO UNDERTAKE
DRAINAGE WORKS .
1.--(1) The council of each county in Northern
Irelandotherthan a county borough (inthisAct referredto as " the county council" )shallbe a drainageauthority
forthe purposesofdrainingany landswithintheircounty
which areliabletobe floodedorinjuredby water,orwhose
drainage iscapable of being improved ; and , subjectto
the provisionsof thisAct,the county councilshallhave
power-
(a) to undertake,constructand maintain allsuch
drainage works and do allsuch things as are
described in the First Schedule to this Act
in accordance with schemes prepared by the
county council and confirmed under this
section ;
(b) to cause such surveys,reportsand plans to be
made as may be necessaryfor the purpose of
preparingany schemes under thissectionand
constructingand maintaining the drainage
works so undertaken ; and
(c) to appoint such officersand servants, execute
such works, and do allsuch other things as
may be necessary for the purposes of their
powers and duties under this Act and be
sanctionedby the Ministryof Home Affairs.

## Page 189

[15 & 16 GEO .5.] 183Drainage Act [Ch .24.]
(Northern Ireland), 1925.
(2) A scheme under thissectionshallmake pro-
visionwith respectto allsuch matters and thingsas are
requiredto be provided for and done,in orderto enable
the county councilto carryout the scheme in accordance
with the provisionsof thisAct .
(3) Where a scheme for undertaking drainage
works embodies an agreement enteredintowiththeseveral
occupiersof the lands to be drained or improved by
drainage for the recovery from those occupiersof the
costof carryingout and maintainingthe drainageworks,
and does not contain any provisionsfor the acquisition
of land or for the imposition of a drainage rate, the
scheme may , upon being confirmed by the Ministry of
Home Affairs,but not otherwise, be carriedout by the
county council.
A scheme to which this sub-sectionappliesis in
this Act referred to as " a minor scheme ," and a minor
scheme shall specify such matters and contain such
provisionsas may be prescribed.
(4) The provisionsofPart I.oftheSecond Schedule
to thisAct shallhave effectinrelationto the preparation,
confirmationand carryingout of schemes to which the
lastprecedingsub-sectiondoes not apply, and any such
scheme isin thisAct referredto as " a major scheme ."
Provided that nothing in this sub-section, nor in
Part I.ofthe saidSchedule,shallbe construedasenabling
objectionsto any assessmentofthe value oflandsforthe
purpose of a drainagerateto be made or determined,or
any such assessmentto be revisedor amended ,otherwise
than as is expresslyprovided in this Part of thisAct .
(5) The county surveyor,or any otherduly author-
isedofficerof the county council, may enter upon any
lands and execute all such works and do all such other
thingsas arenecessaryforthe purposesof any scheme
orforthe executionof any drainageor otherworks under
thisAct ,and may make allsuch inquiriesand investiga-
tionsas are necessaryfor the purposes of any surveys,
reportsorplansinconnectionwithsuchscheme orworks;
and the county council shall make reasonable com-
pensation,subjectto the provisionsof thisPart of this
Act, for any injurydone by the county surveyoror
other such officer.

making by the county councilof annual or other con-
tributionsout of the county fund towards any ofthe said
expenses; and the amount of any such contributions
shallbe raisedby means of the poor rate,as a county at
largecharge or as a districtcharge or offsome area less
than a county district, according as the scheme may
provide .
6.-(1) On the completion of any drainage works
undertaken in pursuance of a major scheme , or on the
expirationof the period, or any extended period, fixed
for their completion, the Commissioner of Valuation
shallcause such valuatoror surveyor as may be nomin-
ated by him from amongst the officersof hisdepartment
to inspectthe lands to which the assessmentsfixedby
the scheme for the purpose of the drainage rate relate,
and to report to the Commissioner of Valuation to what
extent(ifany)the assessmentsought to be revised; and
the Commissioner of Valuation shall consider the said
report, and shall, aftersuch notice and afteraffording
such opportunity for the making and hearing of ob-
jectionsto any assessmentas may be prescribed,issuea
certificatefixingthe assessments of the severallands
specifiedin the scheme , having regard to the estimated
increase(ifany)intheirannual value,and to the different
degrees of benefitwhich, in the opinion of the Com-
missioner of Valuation ,the severallands willderive from
the drainage works. The assessments so fixed shall
have effectfor the purpose of the drainagerate for the
localfinancialyear in which the certificateis issued.
(2) The Commissioner of Valuation may , on the
applicationof any person interested, amend any assess-
ments fixedby him under sub-section(1) of thissection
by making such alterationsin any such assessment as
appear to him to be necessaryor proper, and may also,
on the likeapplication, apportionthe assessmentof any
lands as between differentpartsof thoselands;and any
such amendments or apportionments shallhave effect
forthe purpose of the drainagerateforthe next ensuing
localfinancialyear.

SPECIAL PROVISIONS AS TO CERTAIN DRAINAGE
AUTHORITIES .
17.-(1) If any drainage authorityto which this
Part of thisAct appliesconsiderthat itisdesirablefor
the purpose of maintaining any drainage works main-
tainableby them or under theircharge-
(a) to carry out works or provide machinery
which cannot be carriedout or providedby the
drainage authority under any enactment
applicableto them ; or
(b) to provide for the amendment of any enact-
ment which affectsany such works or contains
provisionsas to the manner in which, or the
conditionssubjectto which, the works are to
be maintained ;
then the drainage authority may , after consultation
with the county council of every county within which
the powers of the drainage authorityare proposed to
be exercised, preparea scheme forthe carryingout of
such works, the provisionof such machinery , or the
amendment of such enactment (as the case may be),and
shallsubmit the scheme to the Ministry of Finance for
confirmation, and the scheme shallhave effectifand so
farasitmay be confirmedby the saidMinistry.
This Part ofthisAct appliestothe Lough and River
Erne Drainage and Navigation Board , and the Lough
Neagh Drainage Trustees.

itsapplicationas aforesaid-

may appealunder sectiontwo hundred and sixty-nine
of that Act ; and paragraphs (1), (2), (3), (6) and (7) of
that sectionshallapply accordingly, with such adapta-
tions as may be prescribedby regulationsto be made
jointlyby the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of
Home Affairs under Part IV . of this Act :
Provided that nothing in this section shall be
construed as enabling objectionsto any assessment of
the value of lands for the purpose of a drainage rate
to be made or determined,or any such assessmentto be
revised or amended , otherwise than as is expressly
provided in Part I. of thisAct .

FIRST SCHEDULE .
DESCRIPTION OF DRAINAGE WORKS .
1. Clearingofrivers,watercourses,& c.,thatistosay:-
(a) the removal ofobstructionssuch as fallenor ingrowingtrees
or bushes,refuseor othermaterial;
(b) the removal of shoalsand cesses;
(c) the shaping,trimming and revettingof banks.
2. Works in connectionwith main drainsand theirfeeders,that is
to say :-
(a) the cleansing,widening,deepeningor otherwiseimproving
of existingdrains;
(b) the cuttingof new drainswhere required;
(c) theraisingand repairingofexistingembankments,and the
construction of new embankments ;
(d) the sinkingof pumping sumps ;
(e) the constructionand repairingof sluices;
(f) the removal and disposalof old spoilbanks.
3.Works inconnectionwithagriculturallands,thatisto say:-
(a) the drainingof farm roads and tracks;
(b) the clearingof watercourseson agriculturallands in cases
where,afterthe serviceupon him of a noticeunder Part I.
of thisAct , the owner or occupierof the lands failsor
neglects to scour out and cleanse a watercourse .
4. New construction,that isto say :-
(a) thecuttingthroughof " U " or " S " bendssoastostraighten
and shorten the channel ;
(b) the constructionof new channelsor water-ways and of new
out-fallchannelsto existingmain drainsand theirfeeders;
(c) the re-constructionand improvement of bridges, locks,
overflows, weirs and hatches necessitatingstructural
alterations ;
Section 1,

## Page 208

202 [15 & 16 GEO .5.][Ch .24.] Drainage Act
A.D. 1925 .
(Northern Ireland), 1925 .
(d) the re-constructionofdamaged or inadequatebridgesand
culvertsand the substitutionof new bridgesand culverts
therefor ;
(e) theformationofcattlewatering-places,sheepwashingsand
otherconveniences,theprovisionofwhichiscalculatedto
minimisetheriskoffuturedamage toimproved watercourses.
The referencesinthisparagraphtobridgesshallnotbeconstrued
as includingthe re-constructionof a damaged bridge, or buildingof
a new bridge,whichisa publicwork to whichtheLocalGovernment
Acts (NorthernIreland),1898to 1924,apply.
5. Removal or alterationof artificialobjectssuch as weirs,sluices,
mills, dams ,& c.
6. Such otherclassesof works as may be consideredby the Drainage
Advisory Committee to be analogousto any classesof works
described in this schedule .

SECOND SCHEDULE .
PART I.
PREPARATION AND CONFIRMATION OF MAJOR SCHEMES .
1. The scheme shallspecify-
(a) the lands to be drained or improved by drainage and the
ocoupiersthereof;
(b) the detailsof the works proposedto be carriedout ;
(c) the increaseof annual value accordingto which the lands
are to be assessed to the drainage rate ;
(d) where itisproposedto constitutea drainagedistrict, the
area to be so constituted ;
(c) where itisproposed to acquireland, the land proposed to
be acquiredwhether by agreement or compulsorily;
(f) an estimateofthe costof the scheme and of the amount of
the drainage rate proposed ;
(g) such othermattersas may be prescribedin thatbehalf.
2. The scheme shallcontainallsuch provisionsas may be
necessary :-
(a) fortheraisingand recoveringof theexpensesof carrying
out the scheme and maintainingthe works when completed;
(b) forthe appointment, where any area isproposedto be
constitutedasa drainagedistrict,of a drainagecommittee
or jointcommitteeforthat area, and forregulatingthe

## Page 209

[15 & 16 GEO .5.] 203Drainage Act [Ch .24.]
(Northern Ireland),1925 .
qualificationsand term of officeof the members of the A.D. 1925.
committee,the representationofthecounty councilthereon,
and the exerciseand performanceby the committee of their
powers and dutiesunder the scheme ;
(c) ifthe drainagecommittee isto consistin whole or in part
of electedmembers , for the holding of electionsand for
prescribingthepersonsby whom ,and themanner inwhich,
the members are to be elected ;
(d) in the case of the transferof any drainagebusinessto the
countycouncilunderPartII.of thisAct,forthe matters
requiredto be providedfor in relationto the transferand
carryingout of such business;
(e) generally,forallsuchmattersasrequireto be providedfor
inordertoenablethecountycounciltocarryoutthescheme
in accordancewith the provisionsof thisAct.
3. Noticeofthe scheme and of thetime (not beinglessthan
twenty-one days)withinwhich objectionsto the scheme must be sent
to the Ministryof Home Affairsshallbe given to such personsand in
such manner as may be prescribed.
4. On the expirationof the time limitedforsendingobjections,
the Ministryof Home Affairs,afterconsideringany objectionsthat
may have been duly sent to that Ministry,may make an ordercon-
firmingthe scheme with or without modifications,or may rejectthe
scheme .
5. The scheme shall not take effect unless and until it is con-
firmedby the Ministryof Home Affairs,but when so confirmedshall
become finaland have effectas ifenacted in thisAct ; and the con-
firmationby the Ministryof Home Affairsshallbe conclusiveevidence
that the requirementsof thisAct have been complied with and that
the scheme has been duly made and iswithinthe powers of thisAct.
PART II .
PROVISIONS AS TO THE COMPULSORY ACQUISITION
OF LAND UNDER A MAJOR SCHEME .
1. The county council, where they propose to purchase land
compulsorilyunderthescheme,may make and submittothe Ministryof
Home Affairsan orderauthorisingthecounty councilto put inforceas
respectsthe land specifiedin the order the provisionsof the Lands
ClausesActs withrespecttothe purchaseand takingoflandsotherwise
than by agreement.
2. An order under this Part of this Schedule shall be of no force
unlessand untilitisconfirmedby the Ministryof Home Affairs,and
that Ministrymay confirm the order eitherwithout modificationor
subjectto such modificationsas itthinksfit,and an order,when so
confirmed, on the expirationof one month from the publicationof
noticeof confirmation,shallhave effectas partof the scheme .
3. The ordershallbe in the prescribedform and shallcontain
such provisionsas may be prescribedforthe purpose of carryingthe
order intoeffectand shallincorporate,subjectto the necessaryadapta-
tions,the Lands ClausesActs as definedinthispart ofthisSchedule.

PROVISIONS AS TO PUBLIC INQUIRIES BY THE
MINISTRY OF FINANCE .
1. The Ministry of Finance (in thisSchedule referredto as
" the Ministry")shallappointa personor personsto hold the inquiry.
2. The person or persons so appointed shallhold sittingsin
some convenientplace, and thereatshallhear, receiveand examine
any evidenceand informationoffered,and hear and inquireinto the
objectionsorrepresentationsmade respectingthesubjectmatterof the
inquiry,with power from time totime to adjournany sitting.
3. Notice shallbe publishedin such manner as the Ministry
may directof every such sitting,except an adjourned sitting, seven
days at leastbeforethe holdingthereof.

authorityconcernedwiththe subjectmatterof the inquiryand,on

ofthe inquiry,shallbe liableon summary convictionto a penaltynot

Provided that no person shallbe requiredto attend beforethe

ofhisattendancehave been paid or tenderedto him .

charges . [22nd December ,1925.]
B E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,

shallhave effectaccordingly.

15, 15 & 16 GEORGE 5.
CHAPTER i.
An Act to confirm a Provisional Order of the
Ministry of Home Affairsfor Northern Ireland
relatingto the County Borough of Londonderry .
[9th June , 1925.]
Whereas the Ministry of Home Affairs for
Northern Ireland has made the Provisional Order set out
in the Schedule heretounder the provisionsofthe Public
Health (Ireland) Act,1878 :
And whereas it is requisitethat the said Order
should be confirmed by Parliament :
Be it therefore enacted by the King's most
Excellent Majesty, and the Senate and the House of
Commons of Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament
assembled,and by the authorityofthesame ,asfollows:-
1. The Order set out in the Schedule hereto shall
be and the same is hereby confirmed and allthe pro-
visionsthereofshallhave fullvalidityand force.
A.D. 1925 .

confirmed.

County Borough ) Act (Northern Ireland), 1925.

CHAPTER iii.
An Act to consolidate the local rates leviable in
the City of Belfast: to authorisethe execution
of street improvements and the acquisition of
lands:and forotherpurposes. [9thJune ,1925.]
Whereas the City of Belfast (in this Act called
" the City") is a County Borough subjectto the Acts
relatingto municipal corporationsin Northern Ireland
and the Lord Mayor Aldermen and Citizensof the City
(in this Act called" the Corporation") acting by the
Councilare the urban sanitaryauthorityforthe district
thereof :
And Whereas the several local Acts and Orders
mentioned in the First Schedule to this Act are in force
within the City which Acts and Orders are in thisAct
referredto collectivelyas " the former Acts " and each
of them separatelyas an Act or Order of the year in
which the same was passed or made :
And Whereas the expenses of the Corporation
whether as a municipalor sanitaryauthorityor otherwise
are payable out of the poor rate or out of the borough
fund and the borough rate or the policefund and the
policerateor the generalpurposesfund and the general
purposes rateand itisexpedient that allthe said rates
should be consolidated into one rate and that all the
expensesofthe Corporationshould be defrayedout ofthe
poor rate and out of one fund to be established for the
purposes thereof :
And Whereas itisexpedient that the Corporation
should be authorised to make the street works in this
Act described and to exercise in relation thereto the
powers by thisAct conferred:
And Whereas itisexpedient that the Corporation
should be empowered to acquire compulsorilyfor the
purposes of thisAct and other purposes and to hold and.
deal with lands :

visions in this Act contained should be enacted :
